## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics modeled by ODE rate laws. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are empirical or mechanistic rate laws where the reaction rate depends on concentration, possibly with explicit time-dependent rate coefficients (e.g., changing conditions or catalyst activity).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate production or depletion over time)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition analog)
- First-order with source term: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net source plus linear loss/gain; leads to exponential approach/blowup)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or recombination)
- General power-law rate (nth order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical kinetics / lumped mechanism)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady concentration c1)
- Reversible first-order to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (forward constant source balanced by first-order removal; equilibrium at A = c0/(c1))
- Autocatalytic / self-limiting kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (growth at low A, depletion near capacity c1)
- Time-varying first-order (exponentially changing rate coefficient): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate accelerates/slows due to changing conditions over time)
- Aging/transport-limited rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (t + c1) (effective rate decreases with time due to depletion, fouling, or diffusion-layer growth)
- Periodically forced kinetics (e.g., light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (oscillatory driving of reaction rate)
- High-concentration saturation in driving term: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * A)) (rate rises with A then saturates; lumped transport/activation limitation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line when plotting dA_dt vs A through origin), it indicates first-order kinetics with a constant rate coefficient.
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 or generally A**n (curved on linear axes; linear on log-log), it suggests bimolecular or nth-order power-law kinetics.
- A nonzero intercept in dA_dt vs A (term like c0) indicates a constant source/production term or background generation independent of A.
- A linear form in (A - c1) indicates relaxation toward a steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1 (sign change around A = c1).
- A factor (c1 - A) multiplying A indicates self-limitation/autocatalysis: growth at low A but slowing and reversing near A ≈ c1.
- Explicit time dependence multiplying A (e.g., exp(c*t), sin(c*t), 1/(t+c)) suggests changing external conditions (temperature program, catalyst activation/deactivation, illumination cycles).
- Rational dependence on time such as 1/(t+c) often reflects diffusion-layer growth or deactivation processes that progressively reduce an effective rate constant.
- Saturating functions of A such as 1 - exp(-c*A) indicate diminishing returns at high concentration (e.g., limited reactive sites or transport/activation constraints).

With the fitted values, c5 and c6 are identical, so the two A^2 terms merge, giving an effective numerator \( -0.09437A^3 -0.24192A^2 +2.5072A -0.7563A^{3/2} -0.5480A^{1/2} +0.0519 \) over \(0.7997A+2.2229\); c8 is comparatively small but not negligible near A≈0, while the other coefficients are moderate and contribute materially. Asymptotically for large A the A^3 term dominates the numerator and the model grows ~\((c4/c1)A^2\approx-0.118A^2\), while for small A it behaves approximately like \((c3\sqrt{A}+c8)/c2\approx-0.246\sqrt{A}+0.023\) due to the nonzero intercept c2 in the denominator.

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A**c2 + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 59

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `-0.11847*sqrt(A) - 0.11847*A² + 0.84638*sin(log(A + 1))`

This contains three distinct basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — a square root term
2. `A²` — a polynomial term
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` — a sine of logarithm composition

The key insight is that `sin(log(A+1))` is a very specific transcendental function. For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce this function (or an equivalent).

Let me categorize the candidates by their basis functions:

**Candidates with only rational functions and polynomials (1, 16):** These are rational functions of A. They cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))` or `sqrt(A)` behavior. Candidate 1 has `sqrt(A)` and `A^(3/2)` but still no `sin(log(...))`.

**Candidates with `exp(A*c)` terms (2-6, 8-9, 11, 17, 19-35, 38, 40, 46-56, 58):** Exponentials cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))`. These are all NO MATCH.

**Candidates with `log(A*c + 1)` terms (8, 14, 42, 43, 51):** `log(A+1)` alone is not `sin(log(A+1))`. NO MATCH.

**Candidates with `sin(...)` terms (57, 59):** 
- **Candidate 57:** Has `sin(A*c5 + c6)` — this is `sin` of a *linear* function of A, not `sin(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions. NO MATCH.
- **Candidate 59:** Has `sin(A*c3 + c4)` — same issue. NO MATCH.

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(...) + 1)` (softplus-like) terms (36, 39, 41, 44, 45, 13):**
- These produce `log(c*exp(f(A)) + 1)` which is a softplus. This cannot equal `sin(log(A+1))`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 12:** Has `exp(c8*t)*log(c9*|A|+1)` — contains `t` dependence that can't be zeroed without killing the log term. Also `log` ≠ `sin(log(...))`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 37:** Has `sqrt(A²+c1)` and `log(A*c5+1)` terms. Products/sums of these cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 6, 7, 10, 18, 46:** Various combinations of exp, log, |A| — none have `sin(log(...))`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 49:** Has `A^c6` which is a power law, not `sin(log(...))`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 14:** Has `sqrt(A²+c3)`, `log(A*c6+1)`, `exp(A*c8)`. No sin(log(...)). NO MATCH.

Let me verify I haven't missed any candidate with a `sin(log(...))` structure. Scanning all candidates... None contain `sin(log(...))`.

Since `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all basis functions present in any candidate (polynomials, rational functions, exponentials, simple logarithms, simple sines of linear arguments, square roots, softplus functions), **no candidate can match the GT**.
